Bioinformatics 29, 2790â2791 (2013)." href="/articles/ncomms6443#ref-CR47" id="ref-link-section-d12427e2485">47</a></sup>, followed by software Samtools version 0.1.19 for SNP/INDEL detection with following criteria: (1) minimum depth=5; (2) maximum depth=100; (3) all mapped reads support a homozygous genotype; (4) minimum mapping quality over 10 (ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 48" title="Li, H. et al. The sequence alignment/map format and SAMtools. Bioinformatics 25, 2078â2079 (2009)." href="/articles/ncomms6443#ref-CR48" id="ref-link-section-d12427e2488">48</a>). SNP/INDELs were classified into genic and inter-genic regions. For those SNPs located in the CDS regions, we determined synonymous and non-synonymous changes after constructing the consensus sequences reflecting the position of SNPs. Furthermore, <i>de novo</i> assembled wild mungbean sequences were aligned against 11 pseudochromosomes of the cultivated mungbean by nucmer in the Mummer 3 software package<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 49" title="Kurtz, S. et al. Versatile and open software for comparing large genomes. Genome Biol. 5, R12 (2004)." href="/articles/ncomms6443#ref-CR49" id="ref-link-section-d12427e2495">49</a></sup>. The similarity between two genomes was calculated and visualized by mummerplot.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec15">Genetic map construction</h3><p>To construct a genetic map of mungbean, we sequenced an F<sub>6</sub> population of 190 RIL by Illumina Hiseq2000 through GBS<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 50" title="Elshire, R. J. et al. A robust, simple genotyping-by-sequencing (GBS) approach for high diversity species. PLoS ONE 6, e19379 (2011)." href="/articles/ncomms6443#ref-CR50" id="ref-link-section-d12427e2509">50</a></sup>. Each individual genomic DNA was extracted and then fragmented by the ApeKI restriction enzyme. After a GBS adapter ligation and PCR, the fragments were validated by the Agilent Technologies Bio-analyzer 2100. The resulting sequence library was implemented in the Hiseq2000 sequencer. The output sequenced reads were aligned to the scaffolds by software Bowtie2 (ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 51" title="Langmead, B. &amp; Salzberg, S. L. Fast gapped-read alignment with Bowtie 2. Nat. Methods 9, 357â359 (2012)." href="/articles/ncomms6443#ref-CR51" id="ref-link-section-d12427e2512">51</a>). The genotypes of 190 RILs in the population were retrieved using the samtools software package<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 48" title="Li, H. et al. The sequence alignment/map format and SAMtools. Bioinformatics 25, 2078â2079 (2009)." href="/articles/ncomms6443#ref-CR48" id="ref-link-section-d12427e2516">48</a></sup>. We collected polymorphic sites among 190 populations based on the set of the read depth thresholds of 5, and the quality score of 30 with allowance of 10 missing genotypes. They were grouped into 10-kb windows, and those windows showing an abnormal recombination were discarded. A polymorphic site with the lowest number of missing genotypes among populations was selected as a representative of each window. The 190 genotypes of the representative polymorphic sites were parsed and then carried onto Joinmap 4. Consequently, a total of 239 scaffolds were anchored to 11 pseudomolecules after constructing the genetic map of mungbean.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec16">Detection of transposable element and repeat masking</h3><p>Transposable elements were detected using the software packages LTR-harverst<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 21" title="Ellinghaus, D., Kurtz, S. &amp; Willhoeft, U. LTRharvest, an efficient and flexible software for de novo detection of LTR retrotransposons. BMC Bioinformatics 9, 18 (2008)." href="/articles/ncomms6443#ref-CR21" id="ref-link-section-d12427e2529">21</a></sup> and TransposonPSI ( <a href="http://transposonpsi.sourceforge.net/">http://transposonpsi.sourceforge.net/</a>) with default parameters. Putative LTR-retrotransposons were annotated by LTR-digest<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 20" title="Steinbiss, S., Willhoeft, U., Gremme, G. &amp; Kurtz, S. Fine-grained annotation and classification of de novo predicted LTR retrotransposons. Nucleic Acids Res. 37, 7002â7013 (2009)." href="/articles/ncomms6443#ref-CR20" id="ref-link-section-d12427e2540">20</a></sup> using a set of hmm signatures: PF03078.8, PF00385.17, PF01393.12, PF04094.7, PF07253.4, PF00552.14, PF05380.6, PF00077.13, PF08284.4, PF00078.20, PF07727.7, PF06815.6, PF06817.7, PF03732.10, PF00075.17, PF01021.12, PF04195.5, PF00692.12, PF00692.12 and PF00098. In addition, the hmm of AP_ty1copia and AP_ty3gypsy elements was built using their alignment information from GyDB<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 52" title="Llorens, C. et al. The Gypsy Database (GyDB) of mobile genetic elements: release 2.0. Nucleic Acids Res. 39, D70âD74 (2011)." href="/articles/ncomms6443#ref-CR52" id="ref-link-section-d12427e2544">52</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec17">Gene prediction and annotation</h3><p>The mungbean genome gene prediction was implemented using the MAKER pipeline<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 22" title="Cantarel, B. L. et al. MAKER: an easy-to-use annotation pipeline designed for emerging model organism genomes. Genome Res. 18, 188â196 (2008)." href="/articles/ncomms6443#ref-CR22" id="ref-link-section-d12427e2556">22</a></sup>. Transcriptomes of mungbean from four different tissues of leaf, flower, root and pod were sequenced by Illumina Hiseq2000 and assembled by software Trinity<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 53" title="Grabherr, M. G. et al. Full-length transcriptome assembly from RNA-Seq data without a reference genome. Nat. Biotechnol. 29, 644â652 (2011)." href="/articles/ncomms6443#ref-CR53" id="ref-link-section-d12427e2560">53</a></sup>. We pooled <i>de novo</i> transcriptome assemblies and removed the redundant sequences by software CD-HIT<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 54" title="Li, W. Z. &amp; Godzik, A. Cd-hit: a fast program for clustering and comparing large sets of protein or nucleotide sequences. Bioinformatics 22, 1658â1659 (2006)." href="/articles/ncomms6443#ref-CR54" id="ref-link-section-d12427e2567">54</a></sup>. For the gene prediction pipeline, we used the transcriptome assembly of mungbean, the protein sequences of <i>G. max</i>, and the complete protein sequences of <i>Arabidopsis</i> from Uniprot<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 39" title="Consortium, U. Reorganizing the protein space at the Universal Protein Resource (UniProt). Nucleic Acids Res. 40, D71âD75 (2012)." href="/articles/ncomms6443#ref-CR39" id="ref-link-section-d12427e2578">39</a></sup>. Once an initial prediction was made by the MAKER pipeline, its output results were used for training the software AUGUSTUS<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 55" title="Stanke, M., Tzvetkova, A. &amp; Morgenstern, B. AUGUSTUS at EGASP: using EST, protein and genomic alignments for improved gene prediction in the human genome. Genome Biol. 7, S11.1âS11.8 (2006)." href="/articles/ncomms6443#ref-CR55" id="ref-link-section-d12427e2582">55</a></sup> model parameters for the accuracy of gene predictions. Using the trained model parameters of mungbean, we re-ran the prediction pipeline again against the repeat-masked mungbean scaffolds. A set of the resulting high-confident genes was annotated by software Interproscan5 (ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 56" title="Quevillon, E. et al. InterProScan: protein domains identifier. Nucleic Acids Res. 33, W116âW120 (2005)." href="/articles/ncomms6443#ref-CR56" id="ref-link-section-d12427e2585">56</a>). Furthermore, we used the leaf transcriptome of each species and the protein sequences of <i>Arabidopsis</i> and <i>G. max</i> for the successful prediction of genes in <i>V. radiata</i> var. <i>sublobata</i> and <i>V. reflexo-pilosa</i> var. <i>glabra</i>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec18">TF classification</h3><p>We classified the TF families of the mungbean genome based on the TF classification rules as described in Lang <i>et al.</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 57" title="Lang, D. et al. Genome-wide phylogenetic comparative analysis of plant transcriptional regulation: a timeline of loss, gain, expansion, and correlation with complexity. Genome Biol. Evol. 2, 488â503 (2010)." href="/articles/ncomms6443#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d12427e2618">57</a></sup> Along with the <i>V. radiata</i> var. <i>radiata</i> protein sequences, the protein sequences of 8 plant genomes including 5 dicot plants (<i>A. thaliana, G. max, M. truncatula, C. cajan</i> and <i>C. arietinum</i>) and 3 monocots (<i>B. distachyon, Z. mays</i> and <i>O. sativa</i>) were classified into 101 TF families for further comparative analysis. If the Pfam annotation for plant genome was unavailable in the databases, we annotated the Pfam IDs using Interproscan5.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec19">Identification of non-coding RNA contents in mungbean genome</h3><p>Non-coding RNAs from transcriptome and genomic data were retrieved from database Rfam using software Infernal<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 58" title="Burge, S. W. et al. Rfam 11.0: 10 years of RNA families. Nucleic Acids Res. 41, D226âD232 (2013)." href="/articles/ncomms6443#ref-CR58" id="ref-link-section-d12427e2649">58</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 59" title="Nawrocki, E. P., Kolbe, D. L. &amp; Eddy, S. R. Infernal 1.0: inference of RNA alignments. Bioinformatics 25, 1335â1337 (2009)." href="/articles/ncomms6443#ref-CR59" id="ref-link-section-d12427e2652">59</a></sup>. We made a subset of Rfam members among reference plants, <i>A. thaliana</i>, <i>O. sativa</i>, <i>G. max</i> and <i>Vigna</i> species. The sequences of Rfam sub-members were blasted against the transcriptome and genome sequences with the following threshold settings: number of alignments=5, <i>E</i>-value=1 and sequence similarity= 90%. Infernal were implemented on the matched regions including a flanking 50âbp and transcriptome assemblies to find significance of RNA secondary structure with an <i>E</i>-value cut-off of 0.001.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec20">Transcriptome assembly and <i>Vigna</i> speciation analysis</h3><p>The first leaf trifoliates of 22 <i>Vign</i> <i>a</i> accessions were harvested. Each of messenger RNA was extracted using TRIzol (Invitrogen, Life Technologies, Carlsbad, CA, USA) following the manufacturerâs instructions. All of the messenger RNA samples were converted into a 500âbp paired-end sequencing library to be suitable for a subsequent cluster generation using the TruSeq RNA Sample Preparation Kit (Illumina, San Diego, CA, USA). For RNA sequencing, the Illumina HiSeq2000 platform was used. The short reads were assembled by software Trinity<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 53" title="Grabherr, M. G. et al. Full-length transcriptome assembly from RNA-Seq data without a reference genome. Nat. Biotechnol. 29, 644â652 (2011)." href="/articles/ncomms6443#ref-CR53" id="ref-link-section-d12427e2693">53</a></sup> with default parameters. CDS from the assembly were retrieved by perl script and transcripts_to_best_scoring_ORFs.pl, which was included in Trinity. The redundancy of assembled coding sequences of 22 <i>Vigna</i> accessions was removed from software CD-HIT (ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 54" title="Li, W. Z. &amp; Godzik, A. Cd-hit: a fast program for clustering and comparing large sets of protein or nucleotide sequences. Bioinformatics 22, 1658â1659 (2006)." href="/articles/ncomms6443#ref-CR54" id="ref-link-section-d12427e2699">54</a>). The non-redundant assemblies of 22 <i>Vigna</i> species were clustered using Orthomcl software and found 1,121 shared orthologue loci. For the three <i>Vigna</i> species, <i>V. radiata</i> var. <i>radiata</i>, <i>V. radiata</i> var. <i>sublobata</i> and <i>V. reflexo-pilosa</i> var. <i>glabra</i> that was constructed into large scaffold by <i>de novo</i> genome assembly, we tried to determine the confident orthologues by synteny relationship with <i>G. max</i> and <i>C. cajan</i>. For the allopolyploid genomes, <i>G. max</i> and <i>V. reflexo-pilosa</i> var. <i>glabra</i>, we split the paralogous gene pairs as A and B genome using the recent Ks peak of within-genome synteny comparison and the synteny relationship against <i>V. radiata</i>; using median Ks value of each synteny block, closer synteny block to <i>V. radiata</i> was set as A genome and the other was as B genome. Hence, two OTUs for each allopolyploid species were used to retrieve orthologues. The orthologues of A genome of <i>G. max</i> and <i>V. reflexo-pilosa</i> to <i>V. radiata</i> var. <i>radiata</i>, <i>C. cajan</i> and <i>V. radiata</i> var. <i>sublobata</i> were collected based on synteny relationship finding 173 loci. Finally, common 9 loci was retrieved between the transcriptome-based Orthomcl orthologues (1121 loci) and the synteny-based orthologues (173 loci).</p><p>For estimation of the species tree, we implemented the Bayesian Markov Chain Monte Carlo (MCMC) analysis using the nine loci by the *BEAST option of the software package BEAST version 1.8 (ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 33" title="Heled, J. &amp; Drummond, A. J. Bayesian inference of species trees from multilocus data. Mol. Biol. Evol. 27, 570â580 (2010)." href="/articles/ncomms6443#ref-CR33" id="ref-link-section-d12427e2778">33</a>). We aligned the orthologues of nine loci using software Prank<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 60" title="Loytynoja, A. &amp; Goldman, N. An algorithm for progressive multiple alignment of sequences with insertions. Proc. Natl Acad. Sci. USA 102, 10557â10562 (2005)." href="/articles/ncomms6443#ref-CR60" id="ref-link-section-d12427e2782">60</a></sup>. The analysis was initiated with random starting tree. Analysis consisted with two runs of MCMC with the length of chain being 50 million and the parameters logged at every 1,000 steps. For the substitution model, we run software Prottest<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 61" title="Abascal, F., Zardoya, R. &amp; Posada, D. ProtTest: selection of best-fit models of protein evolution. Bioinformatics 21, 2104â2105 (2005)." href="/articles/ncomms6443#ref-CR61" id="ref-link-section-d12427e2786">61</a></sup> to select the model and we found JTT+G as the best model. For the clock model, we used relaxed clock model with log normally distributed uncorrelated rates. For root time calibration, we used ca. 19 MYA divergence of <i>Vigna</i> and <i>Glycine</i> estimated from chloroplast gene phylogenies of previous study.</p><p>For ML tree, we used the 20 diploid <i>Vigna</i> transcriptome assemblies. Among the orthologous relationship from the Orthomcl result, we retrieved 375 orthologous loci that have one protein for each accession for the concatenation of the confident orthologous loci. The each locus was independently aligned using Prank software<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 60" title="Loytynoja, A. &amp; Goldman, N. An algorithm for progressive multiple alignment of sequences with insertions. Proc. Natl Acad. Sci. USA 102, 10557â10562 (2005)." href="/articles/ncomms6443#ref-CR60" id="ref-link-section-d12427e2802">60</a></sup>. The concatenation of alignments was supplied to Phyml software for ML tree construction with 500 bootstraps<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 34" title="Guindon, S. et al. New algorithms and methods to estimate maximum-likelihood phylogenies: assessing the performance of PhyML 3.0. Syst. Biol. 59, 307â321 (2010)." href="/articles/ncomms6443#ref-CR34" id="ref-link-section-d12427e2806">34</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec21">Identification of disease resistance genes</h3><p>Using the Pfam annotations of the mungbean gene model, we retrieved the two core domains in which they are referred to as NBS and LRR. We used the Pfam IDs PF00931 for NBS domain and PF00560, PF07723, PF07725, PF12799, PF13306, PF13516, PF13504 and PF13855 for LRR domain. For each Pfam ID, the matched protein regions were retrieved and aligned again. The alignment results were converted into HMM of each domain by hmmbuild of software HMMER 3.0 ( <a href="http://hmmer.org">http://hmmer.org</a>). Using our newly built HMM, NBS-LRR genes were searched using peptide sequences of mungbean by hmmsearch of software HMMER 3.0. The functions of the matched peptide within NBS and LRR domains were predicted by BLASTP analysis against Uniprot database<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 39" title="Consortium, U. Reorganizing the protein space at the Universal Protein Resource (UniProt). Nucleic Acids Res. 40, D71âD75 (2012)." href="/articles/ncomms6443#ref-CR39" id="ref-link-section-d12427e2825">39</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec22">Analysis of whole-genome duplication</h3><p>The whole-genome duplication and allopolyploidization of <i>V. radiata</i>, <i>V. reflexo-pilosa</i> and <i>G. max</i> were estimated using the collinearity within each genome. The protein sequences of each genome were initially self-blasted to determine a homologous relationship with an <i>E</i>-value threshold of 1e<sup>â10</sup>. The collinearity based on the peptide locations in the genome was calculated by software MCScanX with default parameters<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 62" title="Wang, Y. P. et al. MCScanX: a toolkit for detection and evolutionary analysis of gene synteny and collinearity. Nucleic Acids Res. 40, e49 (2012)." href="/articles/ncomms6443#ref-CR62" id="ref-link-section-d12427e2853">62</a></sup>. Using the perl script, add_ka_and_ks_to_collinearity.pl included in MCScanX package, we calculated Ks values of the homologues within collinearity blocks. The median of Ks values was considered to be a representative of the collinearity blocks. The divergence times were estimated using the two different rates of 5.17 and 6.1 synonymous substitutions per synonymous site every 1 billion years<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 10" title="Schmutz, J. et al. Genome sequence of the palaeopolyploid soybean. Nature 463, 178â183 (2010)." href="/articles/ncomms6443#ref-CR10" id="ref-link-section-d12427e2857">10</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 63" title="Lynch, M. &amp; Conery, J. S. The evolutionary fate and consequences of duplicate genes. Science 290, 1151â1155 (2000)." href="/articles/ncomms6443#ref-CR63" id="ref-link-section-d12427e2860">63</a></sup>.</p></div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="Sec23" data-title="Additional information"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec23-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec23">Additional information</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec23-content"><p>Accession codes. The mungbean genome assembly, gene models, genetic marker information, annotations, and other related files have been deposited in GenBank/EMBL/DDBJ under the accession code <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/nuccore/?term=JJMO00000000">JJMO00000000</a>.</p><p><b>How to cite this article:</b> Kang, Y. J. <i>et al.</i> Genome sequence of mungbean and insights into evolution within <i>Vigna</i> species. <i>Nat. Commun.</i> 5:5443 doi: 10.1038/ncomms6443 (2014).</p></div></div></section>

                </p></li><li class="c-article-references__item js-c-reading-companion-references-item" itemprop="citation" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/ScholarlyArticle"><meta itemprop="author" content="SM. Defaria, GP. Lewis, JI. Sprent, JM. Sutherland, " /><meta itemprop="datePublished" content="1989" /><meta itemprop="headline" content="Defaria, S. M., Lewis, G. P., Sprent, J. I. &amp; Sutherland, J.               <p class="c-article-further-reading__journal-title" id="journal-name-5">
                <i>Frontiers in Genetics</i>
                (2020)
              </p>
            </li>
          
        </ul>
      </div>
    </div>
    </section>
